185. Re: Few questions from beginner about some techniques
From: "per_fredlund" <per_fredlund@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 30 Aug 2007 09:05:37 -0000

Hi :-)

As an example of "solving all in same layer" i will show how to do a
simple pattern, the 4 T

- put 4 c/e blocks into U with L B R L' F L
- make 4-cycle on them with simply U
- undo first step

>>>> L B R L' F L U L' F' L R' B' L'
it is ALWAYS possible to solve the state(s) with corner 4-cycle and
edge 4-cycle by a rather long U or U' conjugation. In fact both ways
are always possible. If left with sucah a state after som intitial
turns always look for inserting that conjugate at some previous
point, it may be more efficient than just doing it at the end :D So
it's a bit like inserting 3-cycle, but less chance of cancelled turns.

Scramble premoves is closely related to pseudoblocks. To explain the
theory is a bit long winded. I will explain how to use ONE premove.
Making more is just the nesting of doing 1 at a time of course.

186. No Subject
From: Unknown Sender
To: Unknown Recipient
Date: No Date

D B)*x, that is do F then D B x number of times. We now have a pseudo 2x2x= 3 block at UF position. If we had only done D B x number of times we would= have had a perfect 2x2x3 block at UF position. What actually happens here= is a bit like: "i have almost a perfect 2x2x3 block here, i can make it = perfect if before the scramble that layer making the block pseudo had been= in a different position first". This is exactly what we do. We force the = "imperfect layer" to become perfect by changing it before the scramble. No= w we basically solve a different scramble. Fortunately the adjusted scramb= le and original scramble are closely related. And the solution to the adju= sted scramble is transformed to a solution of the original scramble with a= few turns done at the end. For examples see the FMC archives. Cyclical sh= ift is nothing but a particular form of conjugation which you seem to know= about already. If you have a sequence M1 M2 M3 ... ... Mk conjugate it wi= th the inverse of the first move like so: (M1)' M1 M2 M3 ... ... Mk M1, th= en (M1)' M1 obviously cancels. This is a cyclical shift 1 step countercloc= kwise. Further steps are easily achieved by now comjugating with (M2)' and= so on. Cyclical shift the other way is also possible:(different conjugati= on) Mk M1 M2 M3 ... ... Mk (Mk)' where Mk (Mk)' cancels. And so on ... -= Per > --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, "dcserafine" <dcseraf= ine@...> wrote: > > Hi. > > I have some questions. 191. Re: Few questions from beginner about some techniques
From: "Ryan Heise" <ryan@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Mon, 03 Sep 2007 16:34:22 -0000

dcserafine wrote:

> Heise method.
> Sometimes I can't manage with parity in Stage 3. What I mean? I take
> the first pair and permute edges to get four corners left. But in
> some cases I have to switch only two edges in last layer ( or one
> from the middle and one from ll ).

There are a few basic/simple strategies:

{ R2, U } moves, e.g. R2 U2 R2 U' R2 U' R2 (very efficient),
{ R, U } moves, e.g. R U2 R' U2 R U R' U R U' R' (not so efficient).
{ R, U, L } moves, e.g. R U' R' U' U2 L' U R' U' L (not so efficient).

And an advanced strategy:

I still haven't written about this on my page. I am calling it the
"Down-Under" maneuver:

B2 D' R D B2

The free slot is at F-R, the FR edge is at UB, and this maneuver moves
UB into FR by going down (B2) and under (D' R). The BL slot is also
affected, and so you need to prepare that slot before applying the
maneuver.

Among the things that it is useful for is your trouble case above:

L U L' U down-under

Other unrelated examples of its use:

L down-under L'
L U2 L' down-under

--
Ryan Heise http://www.ryanheise.com/cube/

197. Polish Open 2007
From: "arnaudvangalen" <avgalen@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 20 Sep 2007 23:08:46 -0000

With some practise and information that I found on this topic I
improved my personal best from 47 to 37 and then to 33.

On both scrambles I found a 7 move 2x2x3 block. On the first attempt
I got a 13 move full F2L (I used a different approach to do my 37
move solve because I don't know OLL/PLL). On the second solve I
almost got really lucky, it could have been a 20 moves solution if it
weren't for 2 misoriented corners.

On both attempts Zbigniew Zborowski got first place with 33 and 31
moves!

Scramble1: D2 U' R D' U2 L' D' R2 B F2 R2 B' F L' D' B2 F2 D' U B2 F'
D2 B2 D2 L2
F2L in 13 (Arnaud): x y R2 F D F L2 B U2 R2 U F D2 F' U'
F2L in 13 (FURBDL): U2 R B R D2 L F2 U2 F R B2 R' F'
37 (Arnaud): x y R2 F D F L2 B U2 R2, x2 y D U' R U R' U2 R' F R F'
D', y' R' F' L' F R F' L F, y2 F2 U' L R' F2 R L' U' F2 U'
37 (FURBDL: U2 R B R D2 L F2 U2, F B' R B R' B2 R' U R U' F', U' L'
D' L U L' D L, R2 B' U D' R2 D U' B' R2 B'

Scramble2: D' F' D2 L B U2 L2 F' R U2 L2 D B F' D2 R2 D2 R D L2 U' L2
R2 B F'
Almost solved in 20: R' U F' D2 U2 L2 U' L B' L' D' B D2 B2 D2 B R D'
R' D'
33: R' U F' D2 U2 L2 U', L B' L', D' B D2, B2 D2 B R D', U R' U' R U
R', D R U' R' U R U' R' D2





198. Re: Polish Open 2007

Hi :-) I had a quick look at first scramble: D2 U' R D' U2 L' D' R2 B F2 R2 B' F L' D' B2 F2 D' U B2 F' D2 B2 D2 L2 After your first 9 moves: U2 R B R D2 L F2 U2 F i found a nice continuation like so: B R B R' then solve remaining edges and a corner with R D B D' B' R', 2 moves cancel out. Now solve remaining corners with 2 easy 3-cycles like so: R' F' L F R F' L' and B R' U' R D' R' U R D. 32 turns total but surely it's better to insert the last 2 3-cycles :-) Completing f2l is not always the best way to go about it :D Best wishes -Per > --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, "arnaudvangalen" <avgalen@...> wrote: > > With some practise and information that I found on this topic I > improved my personal best from 47 to 37 and then to 33. > > On both scrambles I found a 7 move 2x2x3 block. 200. Re: [fewestmoveschallenge] Re: Polish Open 2007
From: avgalen@... <avgalen@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Fri, 21 Sep 2007 15:14:05 +0200



Thanks for all this info Per, I will study it this weekend. I seem
to be pretty good at finding good beginnings, but I lack the
experience (only 10 FMC's sofar, 31 is my best) and knowledge (4 look
last layer) to make for a very good finish. For me a 2 look last layer
(6/7 + 9/10) is a good ending.

Oh, and the fact that I find a 13 move F2L doesn't mean that I used
it. I throw some edge-control or other moves in there to get a better
last layer at the expense of a worse F2L. I will practise
"edge-insertions" this weekend and I have been a little succesfull
with mispaired F2L-pairs (I don't know if that is a common technique,
I mean inserting 2 corner with 2 edges that don't match, by using an
R2 U2 R2 U2 R2 variation you can fix the F2L and manipulate the last
layer in a very easy way)

Finally I just heard that I got your spot for FMC, does that mean
you are not coming at all to Worlds?

> improved my personal best from 47 to 37 and then to 33.
>
> On both scrambles I found a 7 move 2x2x3 block. On the first
attempt
> I got a 13 move full F2L (I used a different approach to do my 37
> move solve because I don't know OLL/PLL). On the second solve I
> almost got really lucky, it could have been a 20 moves solution if

it
> weren't for 2 misoriented corners.
>
> On both attempts Zbigniew Zborowski got first place with 33 and 31

> moves!
>
> Scramble1: D2 U' R D' U2 L' D' R2 B F2 R2 B' F L' D' B2 F2 D' U B2

F'
> D2 B2 D2 L2
> F2L in 13 (Arnaud): x y R2 F D F L2 B U2
R2 U F D2 F' U'
> F2L in 13 (FURBDL): U2 R B R D2 L F2 U2 F R B2 R' F'
> 37 (Arnaud): x y R2 F D F L2 B U2 R2, x2 y D U' R U R' U2 R' F R
F'
> D', y' R' F' L' F R F' L F, y2 F2 U' L R' F2 R L' U' F2 U'
> 37 (FURBDL: U2 R B R D2 L F2 U2, F B' R B R' B2 R' U R U' F', U'
L'
> D' L U L' D L, R2 B' U D' R2 D U' B' R2 B'
>
> Scramble2: D' F' D2 L B U2 L2 F' R U2 L2 D B F' D2 R2 D2 R D L2 U'

L2
> R2 B F'
> Almost solved in 20: R' U F' D2 U2 L2 U' L B' L' D' B D2 B2 D2 B R

D'
> R' D'
> 33: R' U F' D2 U2 L2 U', L B' L', D' B D2, B2 D2 B R D', U R' U' R

U
> R', D R U' R' U R U' R' D2
>

Date: Mon, 01 Oct 2007 21:55:12 -0000

Hi Arnaud, Nice to hear we will compete in Budapest, since you are now the new Dutch record holder..... As a FMC training I studied the Polish Open scrambles and your solutions. I agree with Per your starting moves are very good. For the 1st round I found a somewhat better continuation after your splendid 13move LL (U2 R B R D2 L F2 U2 F R B2 R' F') 1) cycle 3 edges to prepare for a 10 move LL: L2 B (U' D) L2 (D' U) B L2 (9) 2) then my speedcubing alg for corners: L U' B U' B2 R' B L' B' R B2 (10+1) which give a total of 32 moves For the final (2nd scramble) after your 13th move (so after R' U . F' D2 U2 L2 U' L B' L' D' B D2) I found a good continuation: B' D' B' D' B R D R' D which left a corner-3-cycle. When inserting R B2 R' F' R B2 R' F after your second move (at the dot), cancelling out 2 moves which left 28 moves! I needed 30 minutes to find this continuation. My independant 1 hour solves were: 1st round: R' L' D' L U2 B' D2 L' R' F2 R L2 U' B' U2 B' R B R' B L U L' B L' B' L U' (28) pseudo F2L (19) finishing with a 10 move LL-alg and cancelling out 1 more move . final: D' R' U2 R D R' U2 R . R' U F' U2 D2 L2 U' B2 R D' R' B D B2 D B' L B L' B2 D' B' D B' (29) (corner-3-cycle at the beginning,cancelling 3 moves) So your start was much better than mine.... See ya ;) Gus --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, "per_fredlund" <per_fredlund@...> wrote: > > Hi Arnaud :-) > > For the second scramble i insert (D2 R B' U2 B R')*2 into the dot for > R' U F' D2 U2 L2 U' L B' L' D' B D2 B2 D2.B R D' R' D'. 2 moves > cancel out for a total of 30. 206. Budapest mix
From: "Lars Petrus" <lars@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sun, 07 Oct 2007 10:14:57 -0000

The mix was

L D2 R D' L' B F' L R B' F L2 R2 B L2 R B2 U2 L' R' B D2 B L R

I found a 37 move solution, but wrote it down wrong, despite spending
10 minutes on writing it :(. I doubt it matters, as several people
should have beaten that number.

It's a pseudo 2x2x3 block, so you should do L2 before mixing to see
what's what.

B' L' B2 F L2 B R' B' D2 R2 D

(Pseudo)block with edges oriented in 11 moves is good. This is a
fairly natural continuation:

R' B R B2 R2 B R2 B' R2 B'

(Pseudo) 2 layers in 21 moves. This is what I call Dx2
(http://lar5.com/cube/270/zDx.html) and can be solved with Sune +
Niklas in 13 moves, resulting in a total of 35.

I didn't have that memorized (I do now :), so the best I found (20
minutes in) was a Sune + what I call BH54 (It's number 54 in
Helmstetters list for step 5+6+7):

B' R' B R' B' R2 B + B R2 B L* F' U2 F L' B2 R' + D2

Where "L*" is what I wrote down wrong as "D", because of how I think
about that alg. This is the third competition in a row where I fail to
submit a solution because I can't get the notation right. Very
frustrating, and entirely my fault, of course. I've never been good at
(or liked) notation, and really only learned to use it semi fluently
for FMC a few years back.

Hi Lars :-) After your pseudoblock start you can carry on like so: R B2 R2 B2 R This leaves 6 corners to leave as 2 3-cycles L' F2 L B2 L' F2 L B' then D2 L U' L' D2 L U L' and complete solution with D2 for 33 total, so easy. With insertions it's surely quite a few moves better :-) Best wishes, Per > --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, "Lars Petrus" <lars@...> wrote: > > The mix was > > L D2 R D' L' B F' L R B' F L2 R2 B L2 R B2 U2 L' R' B D2 B L R > > I found a 37 move solution, but wrote it down wrong, despite spending > 10 minutes on writing it :(. 209. Re: Budapest mix
From: "Cyril" <cyrilca@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Mon, 08 Oct 2007 14:42:08 -0000

Hi, My 16-minute solution (add D before scrambling): D2 R U2 F L' F2 [2x2x2] D' R' B D2 [2x2x3] R B 'R 2B' U R U' B' [3rd F2L pair + orients edges] R B2 R' B' R B R' B2 [finish F2L and edges] D' R D L' D' R' D L [finish corners] D [end] I haven't looked for insertions for the final corner 3-cycle yet, but I'm happy to tie the world champion with 35 HTM ;-) Hope I can go to the next WC... Congratulations to Zbigniew ! Cyril --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, "Lars Petrus" <lars@...> wrote: > > The mix was > > L D2 R D' L' B F' L R B' F L2 R2 B L2 R B2 U2 L' R' B D2 B L R >

I DNF-ed during the official event because I couldn't find a good continuation after my start. Guus Razoux Schultz and I tried to find a good continuation after the event, but after half an hour we gave up. I had a look at my notes at home and after 5 minutes I found a good continuation that seems incredible clear and easy right now. I found both the "Best start" and the "Alternative start" during the official event Inverse scramble: R' L' B' D2 B' R L U2 B2 R' L2 B' R2 L2 F' B R' L' F B' L D R' D2 L' "Best" start: R F L' B2 L B L2 B2 D L B' U2 F2 D F2 "Alternative" start: R F L' B2 L B' L D B' U2 R' D' R D F' And this should have been my continuation after the "alternative" start: D R' D2 R D' L D' L' D' L D2 L' R D' L' D R' D' L for a 34 move solution which would have made me the world champion. Hi Lars & others, It was nice to meet and compete you Lars! The FMC competition definitely had a hard scramble, after a few moves that seemed right all remaining blocks or pairs were hard to solve. But with a sub-optimal 2x2x3 block I found a nice 33 move solution after 40 minutes or so. I was so stupid to write it down und check only 3 minutes before the end of the hour because I wanted to do a nice insertion on a 3-corner-cycle wich I couldn't find quickly enough. I made errors writing my first it down and had no time to check & correct. I have to wait another 2 years for my next chance.... My solution after 40 minutes was: premove: D2 2x2x3 block: B' L' F B2 L' B' L' R' D' pseudo F2L minus pair: R D B' D pseudo F2L: R B2 D' R' D R B' LL edges: U F R F' R' U' LL corners & correction: F' U F D' F' U' F D . D2 Total: 33 moves. 215. Per is the master of edges-first FMC method
From: "mirek_goljan" <goljan@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Mon, 15 Oct 2007 20:51:24 -0000

It is a wonderfull 12-moves solution for edges you found this week, Per.
I have a small improvement for the corners. After the first twelve
moves D2 F L2 F2 B U2 D B'. R2 U' L' B', I solve 3 corners starting
with two last moves taking back as B L D' L' D B' D' L D L' and
inserting B U F U' B2 U F' U' B at the dot. You're getting 24-mover
D2 F L2 F2 B U' D F U' B2 U F' U' B R2 U' D' L' D B' D' L D L'.

I plan to try the Budapest scramble soon. Just making sure - was it
one hour competition?

Mirek

218. Budapest World Championship Scramble
From: "mirek_goljan" <goljan@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Wed, 31 Oct 2007 16:13:38 -0000

Hi friends of FMC,
although I didn't attend Budapest WC (unfortunately), I dedicated
one hour today and pretended I'm there. Well, there was no presure
from other contestants and not the exciting athmosphere some of you
enjoyed in Budapest. Here is how I proceded.
To remind you, the scramble was L D2 R D' L' B F' L R B' F L2 R2 B L2
R B2 U2 L' R' B D2 B L R. The very first start I found immediately
looked pretty good:
B' L' F B2 L2 R' D' [D2] The brackets indicate a pre-move. So since, I
scrambled with putting D2 before scrambling L D2 R D'....
This is my kind of standard approach solving a 2x2x3 block first. The
next didn't look that good, so I improved it with D' R2 D. I bet on
this start B' L' F B2 L2 R' D2 R2 D [D2] and solved edges next. After
R B' U' B' U B' R2 B' R B, 5 corners remain. Insertions of 2 3-cycles
of corner cubies were difficult and I ended up with a 35-move solution
after total 30 min 10 sec. The next attempt was [D2] B' L' F B2 L2 R'
D2 R2 D _ R B' R' B R2 B2 R' B2 R' D' R2 .D R' and having 4 corners to
solve. This time the insertions were quick and efficient. At the dot,
insert R2 D' L' D R2 D' L :D and at the colon, insert L' D' R D L D'
R' D.
Putting it together, the solution has 31 moves: B' L' F B2 L2 R' D2 R2
D R B' R' B R2 B2 R' B2 R' D2 L' D R2 D2 R D L D' R' D' R' D2. I
needed 39 minutes even, including double checking. I couldn't find
anything better within 1 hour.
Mirek





219. FMC # 177 - 24move *almost* solution
From: "ericdstalter" <ericdstalter@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sat, 17 Nov 2007 21:05:17 -0000

I got excited when I started solving this week, thought that I was
going to have my best solve ever - 23 moves. I realize that I am
posting my "solution" before the time is up, but because I couldn't
find a better continuation or a good solution. So Thought that I would
post this so that you could see my frustration.

U2 F' L U' F' B D L' F2 D2 B2 D' B D2 B D B' D' B' D B D B D2

AAArrrrgggghhhh!!
oh well,

try again next week.

I gave up after a while and threw the towel in.

Eric

221. Competition FMC
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 22 Nov 2007 14:40:01 -0000

Hi everyone,

I have just recently gotten very interested in FMC and am interested
to try it in competitions. I was wondering if someone could describe
the competition FMC experience?

What I am interested in are how many pieces of paper are you allowed
to have based on the rules? Also how much do nerves come into play?

I haven't yet tried doing my FMC attempts in 1 hour yet, so I will
start that soon to get used to the time pressure as well. But I was
curious to hear of how it feels to do FMC actually in competition and
if anyone has any hints for a beginner FMC'er.

Also I do use insertions so I can see how stickers would be useful,
but I usually just remember the pieces that I need to follow and check
insertions for and look after each turn of my partial solution. Would
it be better to invest in some actual FMC stickers for this?

Thanks,
Chris




222. Re: Competition FMC
From: "per_fredlund" <per_fredlund@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Fri, 23 Nov 2007 10:24:15 -0000

Hi Chris :-) The fewest moves rules in a nutshell: - Find and write down the shortest solution you find to a given scramble within 60 minutes. - Solution length is based on face turn metric (also called half turn metric - R and R2 both have length 1 in this metric) - You are allowed to bring 3 cubes. How to make use of more than one cube is up to the indivisual, i find it useful - i always keep one cube with the scramble set up so i can quickly check i set up the scramble correctly successive times :-) - You are also allowed to bring unlimited extra stickers (for insertions most of all - one may bring paper stickers to write on also, to keep track of cycles ...) - IMHO the rules should state that the organisers must bring a cube with the correct scramble set up (or at least a color diagram on paper) for verification purposes. Experiences. Given 60 minutes only about half the time only is spent actively looking for a solution. The rest is spent to set up the cube over and over again, and to verify the solution is correct. The verification can be a very nerve racking experience :-s Being a faster solver than me gives more time to search for solution ;-) Tips. Do not make many turns without writing down what you are doing. It is surprisingly easy to forget what you just did :-P Work with fixed color orientation - i always have U=white, F=blue Avoid using cube rotations (xyz) in notation, this is very confusing as you "lose" information which face is which color. I always rotate the cube in my hands while examining :D I also avoid inner slice turns entirely, with rare exceptions for using them in simple commutators. Inner slice turns mess with the face-color matching ;-) Same goes for lower case (double outer layer) turns, for exactly same reason as inner slice turns. Do not spend excessive time on finding a good start, though a good start is always beneficial. Know all OLL/PLL algs if you always do a complete f2l!! It is beneficial to know many algs for each case actually to try to find cancellations. Skeleton solution + insertion(s) is in most cases superior to a linear solve (be it a speed method variation or more intuitive). And finally, do not understimate the time needed for final verification. It is better to submit a working "45 turn" solution than a "would be killer" solution with mistakes in it. Strictly UDFBRL notation also makes it easier for the judges to validate :-) Good luck!! - Per > --- In fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com, "cmhardw" <foozman17@...> wrote: > > Hi everyone, > > I have just recently gotten very interested in FMC and am interested > to try it in competitions. I was wondering if someone could describe > the competition FMC experience? > > What I am interested in are how many pieces of paper are you allowed > to have based on the rules? Also how much do nerves come into play? > > I haven't yet tried doing my FMC attempts in 1 hour yet, so I will > start that soon to get used to the time pressure as well. But I was > curious to hear of how it feels to do FMC actually in competition and > if anyone has any hints for a beginner FMC'er. > > Also I do use insertions so I can see how stickers would be useful, > but I usually just remember the pieces that I need to follow and check > insertions for and look after each turn of my partial solution. Would > it be better to invest in some actual FMC stickers for this? > > Thanks, > Chris >

Hi Pe(e)r, :-) I think that "e" should not be there but F' is OK. Yes, 34 is excelent and Guus is the 5-minute winner. In my 1-hour attempt, I found U D F R B' (2) R2 B' R' _ F2 U' L F' U' L' U' (1)_ R' D F' D' R + swap 2x2 corners. Then I spent half an hour finding nothing else, so I returned to this one and inserted U L D L' U' L D' L' at (1). Then I made a mistake and ran out of time :-(. Later, I finished with the second insertion B' R B L2 B' R' B L2 at (2) which gives not very good 31-moves solution. I was too busy this week to work on it more, ended up not submitting anything to Dan's FMC. Hopefully next week will be better. Happy cubing! I > > > > > bet on > > > > > > > > > this start B' L' F B2 L2 R' D2 R2 D [D2] and solved > > edges > > > next. > > > > > > After > > > > > > > > > R B' U' B' U B' R2 B' R B, 5 corners remain. > Insertions > > of 2 > > > > > > 3-cycles > > > > > > > > > of corner cubies were difficult and I ended up with > a > > 35-move > > > > > > solution > > > > > > > > > after total 30 min 10 sec. The next attempt was [D2] > B' > > L' > > > F B2 > > > > > > L2 R' > > > > > > > > > D2 R2 D _ R B' R' B R2 B2 R' B2 R' D' R2 .D R' and > > having 4 > > > > > > corners to > > > > > > > > > solve. This time the insertions were quick and > > efficient. > > > At the > > > > > > dot, > > > > > > > > > insert R2 D' L' D R2 D' L :D and at the colon, > insert > > L' D' R > > > > > D L D' > > > > > > > > > R' D. > > > > > > > > > Putting it together, the solution has 31 moves: B' > L' F > > B2 > > > L2 R' > > > > > > D2 R2 > > > > > > > > > D R B' R' B R2 B2 R' B2 R' D2 L' D R2 D2 R D L D' R' > D' > > R' > > > D2. I > > > > > > > > > needed 39 minutes even, including double checking. I > > > > couldn't find > > > > > > > > > anything better within 1 hour. > > > > > > > > > Mirek > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > > >
237. FMC 5min
From: "guusrs" <guusrs@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sat, 22 Dec 2007 23:47:25 -0000

Hi Per, Mirek,

For Dan's FMC 180 my 5min solve was 45 moves:
D' F' U B2 D' B' U' L U D' L D R U2 L B L' B' U2 B' L' B L' B D' B' D
U' L' U L' U' L2 U L2 B' F L F' L' B F' D F D' (45)
Not very good, I couldn't see nice blocks zo quickly. I started with a
siamese 2x2x2 (14 moves) then two seperate pairs (6 + 7 moves) and a
two fase F2L (18 moves).

My 1 hour solution was 30 moves:
2x2x3: L2 D' F' U L D' B' R (8)
F2L-pair: L2 D' F' L' F D2 L' (15)
F2L + smooth LL: D' L B D2 B' L' D L D R' D L' D' R D (30)

Do you have solutions for FMC180?

Greetz;)

Gus


PS. Per thanx for correcting my previous solution. Working precisely
is my weakest point.




238. Re: FMC 5min
From: "mirek_goljan" <goljan@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Mon, 24 Dec 2007 17:16:50 -0000

Hi, after starting with some 5-min practicing I knew 5 minutes is too short for me when I have to write moves down. The best 2 out of about 30 trials were below 30 and the worst were close to 50 moves and over time. The FMC 180 I finished as one of the worst and over time as well. Then I tried it second time: D' U2 R2 F B R L U' B' L2 B' U2 L B L F' L2 F L' F' L F L(23) + 11 moves for the edge 3-cycle. In 1-hour span I did not find anything better than inserting this 3- cycle: D' U2 R2 F B R L U' B' L2 B' U2 L (U B F' L2 B' F U) B L F' L2 F L' F' L F L (30). I would prefer to expand the 5-minutes to 10-minutes if you agree. Still just one trial, no moves taking back, time does not include scrambling but includes writing the solution down. Happy holiday! B' (8) pseudo F2L + LL edges: D R2 D R' D' R' B R2 B' D' R' D R' D' R (23) undo pseudoness: F2 U2 (25) at dot (after move 7) insert: F' U B2 U' F U B2 U' Shall we start a 10 week competition starting from FMC 182? 243. Re: FMC 5min
From: "mirek_goljan" <goljan@...>
To: fewestmoveschallenge@yahoogroups.com
Date: Mon, 31 Dec 2007 16:59:27 -0000

Hi gu(y)s, I agree with all good ideas you came up with the last week. I am willing to get a Google account and fill in a shared excel spreadsheet that Lars wants to prepare. Ten consecutive FMC solved in 10 minutes should not be a problem to anybody while spending 1- hour every week could be a bit more difficult for some. I suggest that one can skip one week of two and catch up later. We trust each other anyway and we agree not to work on (or look at others solutions) any FMC until the 1-hour attempt is finished and recorded. So, 10 weeks, two longest and two shortest out of 10 solutions will not be counted (for each contestant) in the final average of 6. For Per, 12 would take 3 months, so we agree on 10, OK. We count in HTM, i.e. B2 is one move, R'L are two moves. We can see later if other metric would have helped somebody. For example, counting R F R' as one move (HaHa :-), just kidding). BTW, my last challenge in 10 minutes was not lucky again. L2 B' R2 L F D2 F' L2 F'_ L U L B' U' B L' F2 U2 F' U' F U' F2 D' B' U' B' R B R' U B L U' R U2 L' U L U2 L' R' (42 moves, in 7min 12sec). 1-hour: R' D' R' D. L2 U _ L2 F2 R' D F L' B D2 B' L' F B' U2 B2 F' L D L' D2 B', insert D' B D F' D' B' D F at the dot (32). Happy and lucky cubing!
